Summary: 
Germanischer Lloyd Certification GmbH (GLC) has performed the pre-CDM VCS combined validation + 
verification of the project “Bantargebang Landfill Gas Management & Power Generation” in Indonesia 
(West Java Province) with regard to the relevant requirements for VCS project activities. 
The project was designed with the objective to capture, flare and utilise landfill gas (LFG; which is rich 
in  methane  /  CH
4
)  generated  at  the  Bantargebang  Landfill  in  order  to  avoid  emissions  of  methane  to  
the  atmosphere  and  generate  renewable  electricity  to  be  exported  through  the  grid.  Additionally,  the  
Project Activity aims to improve the management of the landfill and its infrastructure. 
This  is  the  combined  validation  +  1
st
  verification  of  the  project  under  VCS  (Verified  Carbon  Standard)  
program which covers the period from 2011-02-26 to 2012-07-31 (both days are included). The project 
is verified against the VCS Version 3
/2/
. The verification is based on the monitoring plan of the drafted 
VCS Project Description document (VCS PD)
/1/
, the Project Design Document 
/15/
 (PDD) as per Clean 
Development  Mechanism,  the  requirements  of  VCS  (VCS  Standard  and  VCS  Program  Guide  of  VCS  
Version 3)
/2/
 , CDM Validation and Verification Standard
/3/
, and VCS Validation and Verification Manual 
/61/
.  The  project  was  validated  and  registered  with  reference  no.  6486  under  the  CDM  (Clean  
Development Mechanism), on 2012-07-05. 
The project activity has already been validated by TÜV NORD CERT GmbH and registered as a CDM 
project  on  2012-07-05.  GLC  conducted  the  additional  validation  of  the  cover  page  and  sections  1.2,  
1.3,  1.5,  1.6,  1.7,  1.9,  1.10,  1.12.1,  1.12.2,  1.12.3,  1.12.4  and  1.13  set  out  in  the  VCS  Project  
Description  for  project  validation  under  Verified  Carbon  Standard.  The  starting  date  of  the  crediting  
period  of  the  project  activity  is  2011-02-26.  The  emission  reductions  are  claimed  as  Verified  Carbon  
Units (VCUs) under the Verified Carbon Standard Program in its version 3. 
The methodology applied for the project to estimate the GHG emission reduction is ACM0001 (version 
11)  “Consolidated  baseline  and  monitoring  methodology  for  landfill  gas  project  activities”.  Monitoring  
report  (MR)
/4/
,  Emission  reduction  calculation  spread  sheets  (ER  sheets)
/5/
,  Project  Description  
document  (VCS  PD)
/1/
  and  other  supporting  documents  have  also  been  made  available  to  the  
verification team by project participants. 
The  combined  validation  +  verification  scope  is  defined  as  an  independent  review  and  ex  post  
determination by the validation/verification body (VVB) of the monitored reductions in GHG emissions 
during  the  verification  period  from  2011-02-26  to  2012-07-31,  and  consisted  of  the  following  three  
phases:  
- desk review of project design, baseline and monitoring plan;  
- follow-up on-site visit and interviews with project stakeholders; 
- resolution of outstanding issues and the issuance of the final verification report and opinion.  
The  overall  verification,  from  Contract  Review  to  Verification  Report  &  Opinion,  was  conducted  using  

                                 VERIFICATION REPORT: VCS Version 3   
v3.2 
4
Germanischer Lloyd Certification GmbH internal procedures. 
A risk based approach has been followed in this verification. In the course of verification (as a result of 
both  a  desk  review  and  an  on-site  visit),  38  Corrective  Action  Requests  (CAR),  18  Clarification  
Requests  (CL)  and  1  Forward  Action  Request  (FAR)  have  been  raised.  All  the  CARs  and  CLs  have  
been closed out successfully
1
. 
As a result of the verification, the GLC's Assessment Team confirms that the GHG emission reduction 
in the verification period from 2011-02-26 to 2012-07-31 (including both days), is 281,951 tCO
2
e. 
GLC does not assume any responsibility towards the issuance and utilization of VCUs hereby verified 
and  certified.  Request  for  issuance  of  VCUs  shall  be  made  by  the  project  proponent  to  an  approved  
VCS  Program  Registry  based  on  the  requirements  set  out  under  the  most  recent  version  of  the  VCS  
Program  Guidelines  clause  on  VCS  Registration.  The  verification  of  reported  emission  reductions  is  
based on the information made available to GLC and the engagement conditions detailed in this report. 
Hence, GLC cannot be held liable by any party for decisions made or not made based on this report.

site visit.

1          INTRODUCTION          
PT Navigat Organic Energy Indonesia has commissioned Germanischer Lloyd Certification GmbH (GLC) 
to  carry  out  the  combined  validation  +  1
st
  verification  of  the  emission  reductions  reported  for  the  project  
activity  “Bantargebang  Landfill  Gas  Management  &  Power  Generation”  (yet  to  be  registered  under  the  
VCS scheme) with regard to the relevant requirements for VCS program as per the VCS version 3
/2/
.  
This combined validation + verification report summarizes: 
(i) The findings from the VCS combined validation + verification for the current monitoring period 
from 2011-02-26 to 2012-07-31; and  
(ii) VCU certification statement for the emission reductions. 
For validation part, refer to chapter 2. 
1.1       Objective       
VCS  Verification  is  the  independent  review  and  ex  post  determination  by  a  Verification  Entity  or  
Designated  Operational  Entity  (DOE)  (which  is  approved/registered  as  a  verifier  by  VCSA)  of  the  
monitored  reductions  in  GHG  emissions  that  have  occurred  as  a  result  of  the  registered  VCS  project  
activity during the defined verification period.  
VCS  Certification  is  the  written  assurance  by  a  Certification  Entity  (which  is  approved/  registered  as  a  
certifier by VCSA) that, during a specific period in time, a project activity achieved the emission reductions 
as verified.  
The   objective   of   this   verification   was   to   verify   and   certify   emission   reductions   reported   for   the   
“Bantargebang Landfill Gas Management & Power Generation” project for the monitoring period covering 
from 2011-02-26 to 2012-07-31 (both days included). 
One of the objectives is also to confirm that the monitoring system is implemented and fully functional to 
generate Verified Carbon Units (VCUs) without any double counting. 
1.2       Scope       and       Criteria       
The scope of the verification is: 
- To verify that the project activity has been implemented and operated as per the latest version of 
the  VCS  PD  and  that  all  physical  features  (technology,  project  equipment,  and  monitoring  and  
metering equipment) of the project are in place. 
-  To  verify  that  actual  monitoring  systems  and  procedures  are  in  compliance  with  the  monitoring  
systems  and  procedures  described  in  the  monitoring  plan  as  per  the  latest  version  of  the  VCS  
PD. 
- To evaluate the GHG emission reduction data and express a conclusion with a reasonable level 
of  assurance  about  whether  the  reported  GHG  emission  reduction  data  is  free  from  significant  
misstatement. 

                                 VERIFICATION REPORT: VCS Version 3   
v3.2 
8
- To verify that the reported GHG emission data is sufficiently supported by evidence. 
The verification shall ensure that reported emission reductions are complete and accurate in order to be 
certified.  
The  project  design,  its  eligibility  as  a  CDM  project  activity  and  the  correct  application  of  the  Approved  
Consolidated Methodology ACM0001 “Consolidated baseline and monitoring methodology for landfill gas 
project  activities”(  version  11)  
/7/
  have  all  been  already  validated  by  the  DOE  TÜV  NORD  CERT  GmbH  
(Report No.: 8000374274-09/272, dated 2012-06-22) 
/6/
.  
As  stated  in  the  Validation  Report  for  the  project  “Bantargebang  Landfill  Gas  Management  &  Power  
Generation”, the validation opinion of TÜV NORD is that the project as described in the registered CDM-
PDD (version 2 dated 2012-06-21 
/15/
) meets all relevant UNFCCC requirements for the CDM, all relevant 
host   country   criteria   and   correctly   applies   the   Approved   Consolidated   Methodology   ACM0001   
“Consolidated baseline and monitoring methodology for landfill gas project activities”( version 11) 
/7/
. 
While the project “Bantargebang Landfill Gas Management & Power Generation” was already previously 
validated as a CDM project activity, VCSA recognizes the CDM as a GHG Program that meets its VCU 
Verification  Criteria.  This  verification  report,  as  required  by  applicable  guidance  of  the  VCS  Program  
Guide 
/2/
,  includes  the  validation  of  additional  VCS  specific  and  unique  requirements  in  terms  of  project  
design, applicability to the adopted methodology and additionality demonstration that were not previously 
assessed/validated in the Validation Report 
/6/
 as per CDM rules and requirements. 
According  to  VCS  3,  the  Project  registered  under  CDM  program  is  eligible  to  claim  Voluntary  Carbon  
Units  (VCUs)  generated  prior  to  the  registration  date  under  CDM  program.  Based  on  VCS  3,  GLC  has  
conducted additional validation that covers validation of the following items of the VCS Project Description 
document 
/1/
: 
Cover page and sections 1.2, 1.3, 1.5, 1.6, 1.7, 1.9, 1.10, 1.12.1, 1.12.2, 1.12.3, 1.12.4 and 1.13  
The validation opinion of GLC is that the Project Activity “Bantargebang Landfill Gas Management & 
Power Generation” as described in the CDM PDD 
/15/
 and VCS PD of 2012-12-03 
/1/
 meets all VCS 
Program requirements as set out in the VCS Rules. 
1.3       Level       of       assurance       
As  the  VCS  Version  3  only  recognizes  verified  emission  reductions,  GLC  has  focused  on  providing  a  
reasonable  level  of  assurance  that  the  emission  reduction  calculation  methodology  used  is  appropriate  
and correctly applied, and that emission reductions have been accurately monitored. 
In  accordance  with  the  recommendations  in  the  Validation  and  Verification  Standard  
/3/
  and  VCS  
Validation  and  Verification  Manual  
/61/
,  GLC  may  discount  verified  emission  reductions  or  requests  a  
discount of these by using conservative assumptions for uncertainties in emission reduction calculations 
that  cannot  be  fully  quantified  or  that  cannot  give  a  desired  level  of  assurance.  For  verifying/certifying  
VCUs,  the  desired  level  of  assurance  was  based  on  the  combined  quantitative  assessment  of  the  
accuracy  of  monitoring  project  performance  and  the  identification  of  material  risks.  For  this  verification,  
GLC is able to give a reasonable level of assurance.

v3.2

1.4 Summary Description of the Project 
The  project  activity  encompasses  the  collection  of  LFG  generated  at  the  Bantargebang  landfill,  its  
destruction  (by  combustion  in  a  high  temperature  enclosed  flare)  and  its  utilization  as  gaseous  fuel  for  
electricity generation in an electricity generation facility.  
The main purpose of the Project Activity is the utilisation of LFG as gaseous fuel for electricity generation 
in  the  electricity  generation  facility.  All  net  electricity  generated  at  the  electricity  generation  facility  is  
exported through the electricity grid, thus displacing equivalent amount of electricity that would otherwise 
be generated by fossil-fuel sources (power plants) and new additions in the absence of the project activity 
(baseline  scenario).  For  periods  when  the  electricity  generation  facility  is  not  (fully)  operational  or  for  
periods  when  more  LFG  is  available  than  the  electricity  generation  facility  can  convert  into  power,  one  
enclosed  high  temperature  flare  is  available  for  safe  combustion  of  the  LFG  with  the  goal  of  avoiding  
emissions of methane (CH
4
) into the atmosphere. 
LFG  (which  is  rich  in  CH
4
)  has  been  historically,  is  recently  and  will  be  in  future  generated  at  the  
Bantargebang landfill as result of the anaerobic decomposition of municipal solid waste (MSW) disposed 
continuously on this landfill.  
The Project Activity comprises the implementation and operation of a Landfill Degassing system in order 
to  capture,  flare  and  utilise  as  energy  source  the  Landfill  Gas  (LFG)  which  is  rich  in  methane.  LFG  is  
captured on the landfill by a system of vertical and horizontal wells, which are connected to a blower by a 
pipeline  grid  (pipelines  constructed  in  polyethylene).  The  blower  creates  a  negative  pressure  in  the  
pipeline system; a transport of the LFG to the blower is so initiated. Before passing the blower, the LFG is 
conditioned in a “Condensate Filter” in order to remove water drops and contaminants. In a second step, 
the  landfill  gas  is  dried  in  a  chilling  unit,  before  it  is  fed  either  to  the  enclosed  high-temperature  flare  
where  it  is  flared  at  combustion  temperatures  between  1,000  and  1,200  °C  or  to  a  set  of  gas  engines  
converting  the  LFG  into  electrical  energy  (including  injection  in  the  national  power  grid).  While  being  
transported  to  the  flare  resp.  the  engines,  the  LFG  passes  several  monitoring  devices  such  as  flow-
meters (to determine the total amount and the amounts of gas being sent to the flare resp. the electricity 
generation  facility,  including  temperature  and  pressure  sensors)  and  a  gas  analyser  (to  determine  the  
methane content of the gas). The electrical power, generated at the electricity generation facility, is send 
injected via transformers and a medium voltage panel into the national grid (in two different transmission 
lines). The energy needs of the Project Activity are either fed by own production or by consumption from 
the public grid.  
During the monitoring period from 2011-02-26 to 2012-07-31, the Project Activity comprised the following 
technical installations: 
Installed power capacity: Stepwise  increased  up  to  12.782  MW
el
  (this  capacity  has  been  reached  
on 2012-05-25) 
Installed flaring capacity: Designed for a maximum flow of 2,500 Nm³/h of LFG 
Blower capacity   Designed for a maximum flow of 8,000 Nm³/h of LFG 
During the conducted site visit (2012-10-09), the average LFG flow was between 4,000 and 5,000 Nm³/h 
with a methane content of approx. 50 % CH
4
.  

                                 VERIFICATION REPORT: VCS Version 3   
v3.2 
10
As  per  the  registered  PDD  
/15/
  of  the  CDM  Project  Activity,  baseline  emissions  are  calculated  from  two  
different sources: 
1.    Methane  captured  and  destroyed  by  the  Project  Activity  by  combustion  in  an  enclosed  high-
temperature  flare  and  in  gas  engines.  This  amount  of  Methane  captured  and  destroyed  is  
calculated by the multiplication of  
-  the  total  amount  being  delivered  to  the  project  (resp.  the  sum  of  amount  being  sent  to  the  
flare and of amount being sent to the electricity generation facility; whatever is lower will be 
taken for conservativeness reason), 
- methane concentration of the LFG, 
-      methane      density.      
2.   CO
2
-displacement  due  to  injection  of  electricity  into  the  national  grid,  which  is  dominated  by  
energy produced with fossil fuels. This CO
2
-displacement is calculated by the multiplication of  
-  The  amount  of  electricity  injected  into  the  grid  less  the  amount  of  electricity  consumed  from  
the grid by the Project Activity, 
- Emission Factor of the Power Transmission Grid. 
Project emissions are calculated as the methane emissions from the flaring activity and the consumption 
of fossil fuels (if applicable). The emission reduction is calculated as the difference of baseline emissions 
and the project emissions as the leakage emissions are considered as zero for the project activity as per 
the applied methodology. 
The   total   emission   reduction   for   the   1
st
   verification   period   from   2011-02-26   to   2012-07-31   is   
281,951 tCO2e. The emission reduction is calculated conservatively as per the applied methodology. 
Further background information on the project activity can be found in the CDM Project Design document 
(CDM PDD) as well as the Validation report which are available on the CDM website: 
http://cdm.unfccc.int/Projects/DB/RWTUV1340626014.25/view
 
The  project  activity  was  implemented  at  the  Bantargebang  Final  Disposal  Site,  near  the  City  of  Bekasi,  
West Java Province, Republic of Indonesia. 
The project characteristics are as mentioned below:

2.2.1     Gap     Validation     
According to the VCS standard Version 3.3 
/2/
 for projects validated under the CDM, the cover page and 
sections  1.2,  1.3,  1.5,  1.6,  1.7,  1.9,  1.10,  1.12.1,  1.12.2,  1.12.3,  1.12.4  and  1.13  of  the  VCS  Project  
Description  Template  shall  be  completed  by  Project  Participant.  A  validation/verification  body  shall  
undertake a validation of same, which shall be accompanied by a validation representation, to provide a 
gap validation for the project’s compliance with the VCS rules. 
GLC  verified  the  information  reported  in  the  VCS-PD  version  02  dated  2012-12-03  
/1/
  against  the  CDM-
PDD 
/15/
, CDM validation report 
/6/
, Project Host country (Indonesia) LOA

3          VERIFICATION          PROCESS          
3.1       Method       and       Criteria       
The  verification  process  was  carried  out  in  line  with  the  requirements  VCS  Version  3  
/2/
.  In  addition,  the  
verification  team  followed  the  guidelines  of  the  CDM  Validation  and  Verification  Standard  
/3/
  and  VCS  
Validation and Verification Manual 
/61/
. Standard auditing techniques and GLC’s CDM Procedures
/13/
 were 
also applied during the verification. The verification team performed first a desk review, followed by an on-
site visit to review the project realization. 
The verification process was based on assessment of the validated CDM Project Design Document (CDM 
PDD)
/15/
,  the  monitoring  report
/4/
,  emission  reduction  calculation  spreadsheet  (ER  sheet)
/5/
,  supporting  
documents  made  available  to  the  verification  team  and  information  collected  through  performing  
interviews  during  the  on-site  assessment.  Furthermore  publicly  available  information  was  considered  as  
far as available and required. 
The  verification  was  carried  out  on  the  basis  of  the  following  requirements,  applicable  for  this  project  
activity:  
•     Requirements and guidance of VCS Version 3 
/2/
. 
•     Applicable CDM guidelines and requirements, including applicable relevant methodological decisions 
made by the CDM Executive Board.  
•     Other relevant rules, including the host country legislation, 
•     CDM Validation and Verification Standard 
/3/
, 
•     VCS Validation and Verification Manual 
/61/
, 
•     Monitoring plan as given in the registered CDM PDD 
/15/
, 
•     CDM Methodology ACM0001 (version 11): Consolidated baseline and monitoring methodology for 
landfill gas project activities 
/7/

3.4       Site       Inspections       
From 2012-10-09 to 2012-10-12 GLC carried out an on-site verification of the project activity. During the 
visit, GLC’s verification team verified that the actual implementation of the project was as described in the 
registered CDM PDD. Refer to 4.1 for details. 
On-site  inspection  included  review  of  data  and  records,  interviews  with  the  plant  manager,  project  
engineer, shift engineers, operations and maintenance personnel confirming all data sources used in the 
Monitoring Report. 
The main tasks covered during the on-site visit included, but were not limited to: 
•     Verified whether the project was implemented as per the description in the CDM PDD
/15/
. 
•     Confirmation  that  all  monitoring  equipment  have  been  installed  and  operated  as  per  the  monitoring  
plan of the CDM PDD
/15/
. 
•     The  operating  staff  was  interviewed  and  observed  in  order  to  check  the  risks  of  inappropriate  
operation and data collection procedures.  
•     Information  processes  for  generating,  aggregating  and  reporting  the  selected  monitored  parameters  
were reviewed. 
•     Calibration records of all metering equipment were checked and calibration procedure was verified.  
•     The monitored data was checked completely. 
 
3.5 Resolution of Any Material Discrepancy 
On  the  basis  of  the  desk  review,  the  on-site  visit,  follow-up  interviews  and  further  background  
investigation the verification report is completed.  
Findings established during the verification may be that: 

                                 VERIFICATION REPORT: VCS Version 3   
v3.2 
20
i) The verification is not able to obtain sufficient evidence for the reported emission reduction or part 
of  the  reported  emission  reduction.  In  this  case  these  emission  reduction  shall  not  be  verified  
and certified; 
ii) The verification has identified significant misstatements in the reported emission reduction. 
A  detailed  list  of  verification  findings  form  the  draft  verification  report,  which  was  sent  to  the  client  for  
resolution of raised CARs and CLs. 
Nonconformities  raised  during  the  verification  can  either  be  seen  as  a  non-fulfilment  of  criteria  ensuring  
the  proper  implementation  of  a  project  or  where  a  risk  to  deliver  high  quality  emission  reduction  is  
identified. 
Corrective Action Requests (CARs) are issued, if: 
•     the  project  participants  have  made  mistakes  that  will  influence  the  ability  of  the  project  activity  to  
achieve real, measurable additional emission reductions; 
•     the CDM or VCS requirements have not been met; 
•     there is a risk that emission reductions cannot be monitored or calculated. 
Forward  Action  Requests  (FAR)  indicate  essential  risks  for  further  periodic  verifications.  Forward  Action  
Requests are issued, if: 
•     The  actual  status  requires  a  special  focus  on  this  item  for  the  next  consecutive  verification,  or  an  
adjustment of the monitoring plan is recommended.  
The verification team uses the term Clarification Request (CL), which is issued if: 
•     Information  is  insufficient  or  not  clear  enough  to  determine  whether  the  applicable  CDM  or  VCS  
requirements have been met. 
For a detailed list of all CARs, CLs and FARs raised in the course of the verification please refer to Annex 
3.  
 
4          VERIFICATION          FINDINGS          
4.1       Project       Implementation       Status       
On  the  basis  of  the  on-site  visit  and  the  reviewed  project  documentation,  the  verification  team  confirms  
that the project was implemented as described in the registered CDM PDD. All the physical components 
and project boundary are in conformity with the description in registered CDM PDD. 
According to the validated CDM PDD, the CDM start date of the project was 2008-12-05
/15/ /17/
 as on this 
date  the  contractual  legal  and  financial  obligations  of  the  project  developer  entered  into  force.  The  
physical  implementation  of  the  project  reached  its  first  milestone  on  2010-06-30,  as  two  gas  engines  

                                 VERIFICATION REPORT: VCS Version 3   
v3.2 
21
(internal  IDs:  GE-01  and  GE-02)  have  been  successfully  commissioned  
/18/
.  The  2
nd
  big  milestone  has  
been reached on 2011-02-25, as this date has been agreed as Commercial Operating Date of the project 
between  the  involved  parties  
/19/
.  The  day  following  the  before  mentioned  agreement  has  then  been  
defined  as  1
st

dates below the following milestones have been reached within the monitoring period: 
2011-03-04 Successfully commissioning of 2 gas engines (internal IDs: GE-03 and GE-04) 
/20/
 
2011-06-25 Successfully commissioning of flare unit and degassing station

2012-02-13 Successfully commissioning of 2 gas engines (internal IDs: GE-11 and GE-12) 
/24/
  
 
Thus, in total at the end of the monitoring period (2012-07-31), the following capacities and devices have 
inter alia been installed and implemented on the project site: 
- A set of 10 gas engines (internal IDs: GE-01, GE-02, GE-03, GE-04, GE-07, GE-08, GE-09, GE-
10, GE-11, GE-12), providing a total installed capacity of 12.782 MWel. 
- An enclosed high-temperature flare with a maximum capacity of 2,500 Nm³/h. 
- Two parallel lines of gas conditioning units, with a maximum capacity of 8,000 Nm³/h. 
- Several sets of flowmeters, pressure and temperature sensors. 
- A continuous stationary gas analyser. 
- A set of electricity meters. 
- Devices as transformers and medium voltage panels to inject the electricity in the national power 
grid.  
The  project  activity  involves  capturing  of  methane  generated  on  the  landfill.  The  captured  methane  
(landfill gas) is utilized as fuel in onsite gas engines. Any excess landfill gas is combusted in the project’s 
high temperature enclosed flare. This is in line with the description in registered CDM PDD. 
GLC’s  verification  team  has  also  verified  that  all  the  parameters  are  monitored  as  described  in  the  
monitoring plan of the CDM PDD in order to estimate the emission reduction.  
It is noteworthy that due to commissioning, not all instruments and devices have been in place and fully 
operational  on  the  starting  date  of  this  monitoring  period  (2011-02-26).  On  this  date,  the  electricity  
generation facility was able to export electricity to the grid. This was monitored from the early beginning 
on  by  the  use  of  electricity  meters.  The  remaining  instruments  related  to  landfill  gas  flow,  landfill  gas  
methane content and flare’s exhaust gas temperature have been commissioned on 25
th
 June 2011. Thus, 
for the months of February, March, April and May 2011, emission reductions from capture and destruction 
of methane contained in landfill gas are not claimed. For these months, only the emission reductions for 
CO
2
-displacement (through electricity exported to the grid) are claimed and verified. 

                                 VERIFICATION REPORT: VCS Version 3   
v3.2 
22
As per the applied methodology ACM0001 (version 11) 
/7/
, the project boundary is defined as below: 
“The project boundary is the site of the project activity where the gas is captured and destroyed/used. If 
the electricity for project activity is sourced from grid or electricity generated by the LFG captured would 
have  been  generated  by  power  generation  sources  connected  to  the  grid,  the  project  boundary  shall  
include all the power generation sources connected to the grid to which the project activity is connected”. 
Based on document review and onsite verification, it is confirmed that all the emission sources within the 
boundary have been considered appropriately. 
 
Implementation status of the monitoring plan and the completeness of monitoring
 
The verification team has followed two steps to assess the completeness of the monitoring. The first step 
is  document  review  and  the  second  step  comprises  on-site  interviews  and  observations.  As  a  part  of  
step  1,  the  verification  team  has  reviewed  the  submitted  documents  such  as  MR  
/4/
,  ER  sheets  
/5/
  and  
supporting documents stated in Annex 2. The monitoring parameters have been monitored with calibrated 
monitoring equipment as described in the monitoring plan of the registered CDM PDD 
/15/
. It is confirmed 
that  the  monitoring  mechanism  is  effective  and  reliable
2
.  Wherever  a  parameter  was  not  sufficiently  
monitored as per the monitoring plan of the CDM PDD, a deviation was applied by the Project Participant 
and  the  emission  reduction  was  calculated  by  a  conservative  approach.  Please  see  below  sections  for  
details. 
Therefore, based on document review and onsite verification, it is confirmed that all the parameters were 
monitored in accordance with the registered monitoring plan during the monitoring period. In the following 
section, the details of monitoring in accordance with the monitoring plan of the registered CDM PDD are 
assessed.  
It  is  noteworthy  that  the  names  of  monitored  parameters  for  the  flow  rates  of  LFG  have  been  changed.  
The  reason  for  this  is  a  change  of  the  recording  time  interval.  The  PDD  stated  that  LFG  flow  is  to  be  
reported  hourly,  while  the  Project  uses  a  much  higher  data  recording  resolution  (per  minute).  Thus,  the  
index  has  been  changed  from  “
h
”  (hour)  to  “
t
”  (minute).  This  is  assessed  in  compliance  with  monitoring

to export electricity to the grid. This was monitored from the early beginning on by the use of electricity meters.

temperature have been commissioned in June 2011. Thus, for the months of February, March, April and May

Type  of  monitoring  equipment:  Two  LFG  flow  meters  of  the  same  model  were  used  to  
monitor  LFG
total,t
  during  the  considered  monitoring  period.  
The   installed   LFG   flow   meters   are   manufactured   by   
Endress  and  Hauser  and  are  of  differential  pressure  flow-
meter  type,  model  Deltabar  S  PMD  70.  Each  Deltabar  S  
PMD 70 flow meter consists of a flow element and a signal 
transmitter  unit.  The  flow  element  uses  the  differential  
pressure   principle:   A   Pitot   tube   (as   primary   element)   
creates  a  pressure  difference  inside  the  pipe,  which  is  a  
direct measure of volume flow. Two impulse lines carry the 
differential   pressure   to   the   transmitter,   where   it   is   
converted   into   the   corresponding   output   signals.   The   
specifications   of   the   installed   LFG   flow   meters   are   
presented below:

In  order  to  measure  the  LFG  flow  in  normalized  volume  
that   means   at   standard   temperature   and   pressure   
conditions  (0  degree  Celsius  and  1.013  bar),  the  above  
mentioned   flow   measuring   unit   is   equipped   with   a   
temperature sensor and an absolute pressure sensor. The 
values of these two devices are combined with the values 
as  measured  with  the  flow  meters  in  the  project’s  data  
acquisition  system.  The  recorded  and  reported  values  are  
then expressed in normalized cubic meters (Nm³). 

                                 VERIFICATION REPORT: VCS Version 3   
v3.2 
25
The   specifications   of   the   installed   thermometer   are   
presented below: 
Resistance  thermometers  are  sensors  with  the  task  to  
measure  temperature  by  correlating  the  resistance  of  the  
sensor  element  with  temperature.  The  designation  “Pt”  
refers  to  the  material  “Platinum”  used  as  core  material  to  
measure the resistance. The designation of “100” refers to 
nominal  resistance  of  100  ohms  at  0  °C,  thus  these  
sensors   are   called   Pt100   sensors.   The   temperature   
sensing unit consists of the following components: 
- platinum coil fitted into two bores of a ceramic rod 
- wires connecting the platinum coil with a transmitter

Is  accuracy  of  the  monitoring  equipment  as

not   specify   the   accuracy   of   the   monitoring

Yes. 
The  registered  PDD  and  monitoring  methodology  do  not  
specify  any  accuracy  requirement  for  the  LFG  flow  meter,  
the LFG temperature sensor and the LFG pressure sensor 
installed   at   the   project   site   to   monitor   LFG
total,t
.   The   
accuracy  range  for  the  installed  instruments  is  ±0.5%  as  
per   manufacturer’s   information.   It   is   GLC’s   contention   
based on its Sectoral expertise that the use of the installed 
instrument represents good practise for monitoring of LFG 
flow, LFG temperature and LFG pressure. 
Calibration frequency /interval: Yearly 
Is   the   calibration   interval   in   line   with   the   
monitoring  plan  of  the  CDM  PDD?  If  the  CDM  
PDD   does   not   specify   the   frequency   of   
calibration,    does    the    selected    frequency    
represent good monitoring practice? 
The monitoring plan of the registered PDD does not clearly 
specify   calibration   intervals.   However,   the   following   is   
stated:  “Flowmeter  is  to  be  maintained  and  calibrated  
periodically according to manufacturer recommendation”.  
The    monitoring    methodology    states    that    flowmeters    
“should  be  subject  to  a  regular  maintenance  and  testing  
regime to ensure accuracy”.  
As     the     manufacturer     is     not     giving     a     detailed     
recommendation 
/26/
,  Project  Participant  has  decided  to  
perform  yearly  a  service  and  inspection  of  all  devices  to  
monitor  LFG  flow  (including  thermometer  and  pressure  
sensor). If during this check the instrument is found outside 
the   maximum   permissible   error,   a   calibration   will   be   
executed.  
Thus,  the  interval  applied  by  Project  Participant  can  be  
deemed correct.

reasonable to believe that hourly reporting would be

Type  of  monitoring  equipment:  Two  LFG  flow  meters  of  the  same  model  were  used  to  
monitor   LFG
electricity,t
   during   the   considered   monitoring   
period. The installed LFG flow meters are manufactured by 
Endress  and  Hauser  and  are  of  differential  pressure  flow-
meter  type,  model  Deltabar  S  PMD  70.  Each  Deltabar  S  
PMD 70 flow meter consists of a flow element and a signal 
transmitter  unit.  The  flow  element  uses  the  differential  
pressure   principle:   A   Pitot   tube   (as   primary   element)   
creates  a  pressure  difference  inside  the  pipe,  which  is  a  
direct measure of volume flow. Two impulse lines carry the 
differential   pressure   to   the   transmitter,   where   it   is   
converted   into   the   corresponding   output   signals.   The   
specifications   of   the   installed   LFG   flow   meters   are   
presented below: 
 
Specifications of the installed LFG flow meter 
Internal ID  BGB.FIR.0006 
Position Tag FIR90.0 
Period installed 2011-02-24 to 2011-10-05
Manufacturer  Endress and Hauser 
Model  Deltabar S PMD 70 
Serial Number E1058F0109D 
Measuring principle differential pressure 
Operating temperature -20...+85°C 

                                 VERIFICATION REPORT: VCS Version 3

In  order  to  measure  the  LFG  flow  in  normalized  volume  
that   means   at   standard   temperature   and   pressure   
conditions  (0  degree  Celsius  and  1.013  bar),  the  above  
mentioned   flow   measuring   unit   is   equipped   with   a   
temperature sensor and an absolute pressure sensor. The 
values of these two devices are combined with the values 
as  measured  with  the  flow  meters  in  the  project’s  data  
acquisition  system.  The  recorded  and  reported  values  are  
then expressed in normalized cubic meters (Nm³). 
The   specifications   of   the   installed   thermometer   are   
presented below: 
Resistance  thermometers  are  sensors  with  the  task  to  
measure  temperature  by  correlating  the  resistance  of  the  
sensor  element  with  temperature.  The  designation  “Pt”  
refers  to  the  material  “Platinum”  used  as  core  material  to  
measure the resistance. The designation of “100” refers to 
nominal  resistance  of  100  ohms  at  0  °C,  thus  these  
sensors   are   called   Pt100   sensors.   The   temperature   
sensing unit consists of the following components: 
- platinum coil fitted into two bores of a ceramic rod 
- wires connecting the platinum coil with a transmitter

.  The

based on its Sectoral expertise that the use of the installed 
instrument represents good practise for monitoring of LFG 
flow, LFG temperature and LFG pressure.

,  Project  Participant  has  decided  to

continuously improved.

Type of monitoring equipment: A  continuous  CH
4
/O
2
  content  gas  analyzer  unit  was  used  
to  monitor  w
CH4
  during  the  considered  monitoring  period.  
The  installed  LFG  gas  analyzer  is  manufactured  by  NUK  
NENNING UND KRUMM GMBH (Germany). 
The  landfill  gas  to  be  analysed  and  measured  is  taken  
direct from the landfill gas pipeline and fed via the internal 
process  gas  pump  to  the  CH
4
  sensor.  The  methane  gas  
analyser   is   an   infrared-sensor   (IR).   It   records   the   
absorption  of  infrared  rays  caused  by  the  measuring  gas.  
The wavelengths of the absorption bands characterise the 
type  of  gas,  whilst  the  intensity  of  the  absorption  is  a  
measurement   for   the   concentration   of   the   measuring   
components. In contrary to the analysing cells for methane, 
the oxygen analyser uses a paramagnetic sensor. 
The main specifications of the utilized CH
4
/O
2
  content  gas  
analyser unit are presented below:

/O
2

Calibration frequency /interval: Weekly 
/41/
 
Is   the   calibration   interval   in   line   with   the   
monitoring  plan  of  the  CDM  PDD?  If  the  CDM  
PDD   does   not   specify   the   frequency   of   
calibration,    does    the    selected    frequency    
represent good monitoring practice? 
The monitoring plan of the registered PDD does not clearly 
specify   calibration   intervals.   However,   the   following   is   
stated:  “Gas  analysers  are  to  be  calibrated  in  accordance  
to  manufacturer  recommendation.  A  zero  check  and  a  
typical  value  check  should  be  performed  by  comparison  
with a standard gas as recommended by manufacturer”.  
The  monitoring  methodology  states  that  the  “gas  analyser  
should  be  subject  to  a  regular  maintenance  and  testing  
regime to ensure accuracy”.  
According   to   manufacturer’s   recommendation   
/41/
,   the   
calibration interval for this analyser unit is weekly. 
Thus,  the  interval  applied  by  Project  Participant  can  be  
deemed correct. 
It  is  noteworthy  that  during  the  monitoring  period  (from  
2011-02-26  to  2012-07-31)  the  gas  analyser  has  initially  
not  been  calibrated  in  a  documented  way.  In  fact,  first  
documented  calibration  was  performed  on  2012-04-12.  
See below for details (point “Did calibration confirm proper 
functioning of monitoring equipment”) 
Company performing the calibration: Factory inspection / calibration 
NUK NENNING UND KRUMM GMBH / Germany 
/42/
 
On site inspection / calibration
 
Operational  Staff  of  the  electricity  generation  facility.  Staff  
performing   the   inspections   and   calibrations   has   been   
trained  by  the  supplier  of  the  flaring  system,  of  which  the  
gas analysing unit is part 
/43/
. 
Did  calibration  confirm  proper  functioning  of  
monitoring equipment? (Yes / No): 
The  calibration  certificates  were  checked.  Some  of  the  
calibrations  show  deviations  higher  than  the  accuracy  as  
defined by the manufacturer. As a reaction to the detected 
deviations,  Project  Participant  applied  a  correction  due  to  
gas  calibration  drifts  above  1%  accuracy  tolerance.  To  be  
conservative,  Project  Participant  assumes  an  accuracy  of  
+1  %  (instead  of  +2%  as  defined  by  the  manufacturer).  If  
during  an  inspection  the  reading  of  the  methane  analyser  
(while providing a certified span gas 
/45/
 to the gas analyser 
covering  the  range  of  methane  values  to  be  expected  
during  normal  operation)  shows  values  ≥  1.0  %  than  the  
value  of  the  certified  gas,  the  difference  between  1.0  %  
and  the  deviation  is  deducted  from  all  reported  methane  
values for the time between the actual reading and the last 
inspection.   This   routine   is   only   applied   in   cases   the   

                                 VERIFICATION REPORT: VCS Version 3   
v3.2 
39
analyser  shows  a  higher  value  than  the  standard  gas  
(positive  drift),  when  the  analyser  is  over-reporting.  The  
available calibration events, the detected deviation and the 
application  of  a  deduction  due  to  detected  deviation  in  
case of over reporting is listed below:

As  noted  by  Project  Participant  in  the  Monitoring  Report  
and  as  verified  by  check  of  documents  and  conducted  
interviews    by    GLC's    Assessment    Team,    between    
commissioning   of   the   degassing   unit   2011-06-25   and   
2012-04-12,   no   calibrations   are   documented.   As   per   
calibration   protocol   of   2012-04-12   
/44/
,   the   methane   
analyser displayed a value of 55.9 % while being provided 
a  certified  span  gas  
/45/
  with  a  methane  concentration  of  
60.1  %.  This  means,  that  the  analyser  is  reading  4.2  %  
lower than the span gas. An under-reporting (negative drift) 
can  be  stated.  Thus,  Project  Participant  did  not  apply  any  
deduction  from  the  read  values  until  2012-04-12.  During  
the   on-site   visit,   GLC's   Assessment   Team   conducted   
interviews   with   technical   staff   on   project   site.   While   
calibrations   have   not   been   documented,   it   has   been   
confirmed by technical staff that the analysing system has 
been       maintained       according       to       manufacturer’s       
recommendation  (i.e.change  of  filters,  functional  checks,  
removal of condensate). This is plausible as a visual check 
of  the  analysing  system  (intsalled  in  a  switchboard)  by  
GLC's  Assessment  Team  during  the  on-site  visit  showed  
the  system  to  be  in  a  good  shape.  Additionally,  a  part  of  
the installed gas engines rely on the signal of CH
4
-content 
(the  power  load  is  a  function  of  CH
4
-content),  so  it’s  the  
own  best  interest  of  Project  Participant  to  have  a  proper  
signal  of  actual  methane  content  in  LFG  sent  to  the  gas  
engines. Given the cirumstances that the analysing system 
has  been  properly  maintained  during  commissioning  till  
2012-04-12  (period  without  any  documented  calibration  
event) and that it has been found underreporting during the 
first calibration on 2012-04-12, it is acceptable that Project 
Participant  does  not  apply  any  dedutcion  for  recorded  
methane  values  for  the  period  in  question.  For  all  further  
calibration events, the deduction (if necessary) as per table 
above has been applied. 
Is   (are)   calibration(s)   valid   for   the   whole   
reporting period? 
Yes. 
It is notworthy that the first calibration after commissioning 
(on  2011-06-25)  has  been  performed  on  2012-04-12  
/44/
. 
From  this  date  on  till  the  end  of  the  monitoring  period,  
calibrations  have  been  done  weekly  or  in  an  even  shorter  
frequency.  
Given  the  fact  that  for  the  period  without  any  documented  
calibration  (2011-06-25  to  2012-04-12)  the  instrument  has  
been  underreporting  (details  see  above)  and  that  for  the  
period from 2012-04-12 to the end of the monitoring period 
the     calibration     frequency     as     per     manufacturer’s     
recommendation  has  been  applied,  it  is  the  opinionon  of  
GLC's Assessment Team that the calibrations are valid for 
the whole reporting period.

  belongs  to  the

  (Project  emissions  from  flaring  of

/7/
   refers   for   the

/9/

Reporting frequency is not indicated.  
As  per  the  monitoring  plan  of  the  registered  PDD  
/15/
, 
“Temperature is to be logged minimum per minute basis to 
be able to establish its hourly profile”.

  and  monitoring

/7/
.  
 
Type of monitoring equipment: A thermocouple of type “N” is used to monitor T
flare,h
 during 
the   considered   monitoring   period.   This   thermocouple   
consists   of   a   ceramic   protection   tube,   in   which   two   
thermocouple  wires  are  inserted.  These  wires  consist  of  
different  materials  (conductors),  in  which  a  temperature  
difference  between  these  conductors  produces  a  voltage  
difference  between  the  two  substances,  which  can  be  
measured and transferred into a temperature reading. 
The   specifications   of   the   thermocouple   are   presented   
below: 
 
Specifications of the installed thermocouple 
Internal ID  BGB.TIC.0015 
Position Tag TICAH 81.26 
Period installed 2011-06-05 to 2012-08-30
Manufacturer  Jumo GmbH & Co.KG, 
Germany 
Model  Thermocouple Type N 
Serial Number Without any serial number
Measuring principle Seebeck effect 
Maximum temperature 1,200 °C 
Defined up to  1,300 °C 
Tolerance class ±2.5 °C 
Source: 
/50/ /51/
 
 
Is  accuracy  of  the  monitoring  equipment  as  
stated in the CDM PDD? If the CDM PDD does 
not   specify   the   accuracy   of   the   monitoring   
Yes. 
The  registered  PDD  and  monitoring  methodology  do  not  
specify  any  accuracy  requirement  for  the  thermocouple  

                                 VERIFICATION REPORT: VCS Version 3

49
equipment,   does   the   monitoring   equipment

installed at the project site to monitor T
flare,h
. The accuracy 
range   for   the   installed   instruments   is   ±2.5°C   as   per   
manufacturer’s  information.  It  is  GLC’s  contention  based  
on  its  Sectoral  expertise  that  the  use  of  the  installed  
instrument   represents   good   practise   for   monitoring   of   
flare’s exhaust gas temperature. 
Calibration frequency /interval: Yearly 
Is   the   calibration   interval   in   line   with   the   
monitoring  plan  of  the  CDM  PDD?  If  the  CDM  
PDD   does   not   specify   the   frequency   of   
calibration,    does    the    selected    frequency    
represent good monitoring practice? 
The  monitoring  plan  of  the  registered  PDD  does  clearly  
specify   calibration   intervals.   The   following   is   stated:   
“Thermocouple should be replaced or calibrated annually”. 
The  monitoring  methodology  resp.  the  referred  tool  gives  
the same statement.  
It  is  noteworthy  that  the  thermocouple  (commissioning  on  
2011-06-25)     was     scheduled     for     calibration     resp.     
replacement  with  a  new  unit  no  later  than  2012-06-24.  As  
per  statement  of  Project  Participant  (and  confirmed  by  
interviews with operational staff during the on-site visit) the 
replacement  took  place  on  2012-08-30.  This  delay  bases  
on sourcing and transport problems (unit has to be ordered 
in Europe).  
This   delay   in   calibration   resp.   replacement   can   be   
accepted for the following reasons: 
Between 2012-06-24 (date the calibration/replacement was 
due)  and  2012-07-31  (last  day  of  the  monitoring  period),  
the flare was operational for 47 min (of 912 minutes for this 
period).  This  represents  an  operation  of  5  %  for  this  time.  
Additionally, in the period mentioned above, 787 Nm³ have 
been  combusted  in  the  enclosed  high-temperature  flare.  
This is 1.42 % of all gas sent to the flare and 0.0026 % of 
all  gas  captured  by  the  Project  Activity  during  the  whole  
monitoring  period.  It  is  noteworthy  that  the  combustion  
process of the flare is automatically controlled by a second 
thermocouple  (installed  in  the  center  of  the  flare  stack).  
This   control   allows   a   high-efficient   and   low-emission   
combustion    according    to    various    strong    european    
standards. Furthermore, no indication has been found that 
the  flare  has  not  been  properly  working.  While  the  flare  
was  not  operating  continuosly  for  the  whole  monitoring  
period, the thermocouple in question is likely suffering less 
wear and tear than in continuous operation.  
 Finally, given the fact that flare operated only for a limited 
time  (for  2,026  minutes  the  flare  has  been  operative)  and  
within a small period, it is reasonable to accept this delay.  
 
Thus,  the  interval  applied  by  Project  Participant  can  be  
deemed correct. 
Company performing the calibration: Project Participant decided to replace the used unit with a 
new unit.

Monitored Parameter Assessment/ Observation 
Data                         /                         Parameter:
(as in monitoring plan of the CDM PDD): 
Other flare operational parameters 
[no data unit] 
The monitoring is done by defining if operational conditions 
are met. 
As   per   manufacturer’s   specification,   there   are   four   
operational conditions: 
(a) gas flow rate to FL-01 up to 2,500Nm
3
/hr  
(b) combustion temperature 1,000 to 1,200degC;  
(c)  flare  auto  start-up  or  shut-down  upon  detection  of  
landfill gas pressure (equivalent to flow);  
(d)  burner  temperature  regulator  to  maintain  combustion  
range temperature stable within the range.  
Based on document review and on-site interview, 
manufacturer has set during commissioning the setpoints 
for an optimized combustion and this setting is password 
protected. The assessment team thus assumes that flare is 
operating acc. to manufacturer’s recommendation as long 

                                 VERIFICATION REPORT: VCS Version 3   
v3.2 
51
as there is no malfunction in the PLC and the maintenance 
is correctly done. 
One   S-type   thermocouple   is   installed   to   monitor   the   
combustion      temperature.      As      per      manufacturer’s      
specification,   the   flare   can   be   seen   as   operational   if   
combustion  temperature  is  in  a  range  between  1,000  and  
1,200°C.     An     automatic     burner     control     regulates     
combustion  temperature  to  make  sure  it  is  always  within  
the range.  
The   flare   has   been   maintained   as   per   manufacturer   
specifications  and  there  are  no  malfunctions  reported  of  
the automatic combustion. 
Checking the data reveals that there are in total 9 minutes 
where  LFG
flare
  exceeds  the  benchmark  of  2,500  Nm³/h,  
among   which   4   minutes   are   on   2011-06-24   (during   
commissioning)   and   5   minutes   are   on   2011-12-04(on   
which  date  the  calibration  was  done).  No  corrections  is  
deemed necessary due to the following reasons: 
-The  occasions  only  happened  in  evidenced  comissioning  
phase   and   calibration   date;   under   "normal"   operating   
conditions, such an exceeding did not occur. 
- The occasions are very short time, which can be deemed 
as within the ‘materiality limits’; 
-If  we  correct  this  flowrate  to  its  maximum  capacity  of  
2,500Nm
3
,  the  results  would  be  lower  Project  Emission  
which is less conservative than taking the real value: 
a)   The   high   value   for   LFG
flare,y
   is   not   considered   in   
calculation  of  MD
project,y
  as  the  formula  is  taking  the  lower  
value  (comparison  between  LFG
total,y
  and  sum  of  LFG
flare,y
 
and LFG
electricity,y
). 
b)   Additionally,   the   high   value,   combined   with   a   0%   
efficience  and  roundabout  50%  of  methane  creates  high  
PE
flare,y
  which  are  finally  deducted.  As  for  the  period  of  
2011-12-09, roundabout 260 tCO
2
 are calculated as PE 
flare
 
and finally deducted what is more than conservative.

st

Deviations from the Monitoring Plan
 
One deviation from the monitoring plan has been applied by the Project Participant during the monitoring 
period. Description of this deviation and the assessment on conservativeness of the deviation is provided 
below: 
Description of deviation  Assessment by verification team 
Deviation-1 
As per monitoring plan of the registered PDD, the 
parameter “flare efficiency” has to be determined 
on  hourly  base.  Instead  of  determination  of  the  
hourly flare efficiency, Project Participant applies 
a  determination  of  the  minute-by-minute  flare  
efficiency.   As   Project   Participant   applies   the   
default  value  approach  (0%  /  50  %  /  90  %),  for  
calculation   of   Project   Emission   from   Flaring   
(PE
flare,y
),   for   every   minute   the   following   is   
checked: 
-     If  flaring  temperature  is  below  500°C,  the  
Assessment of Deviation-1
 
The “Tool to determine project emission from flaring 
gas containing methane” 
/9/
 requires the following: 
“In  case  of  enclosed  flares  and  use  of  the  default  
value  for  the  flare  efficiency,  the  flare  efficiency  in  
the hour h (η
flare,h
) is:   
- 0%  if  the  temperature  in  the  exhaust  gas  of  the  
flare  (T
flare
)  is  below  500  °C  for  more  than  20  
minutes during the hour h.  
- 50%, if the temperature in the exhaust gas of the 
flare  (T
flare
)  is  above  500  °C    for  more  than  40  

                                 VERIFICATION REPORT: VCS Version 3   
v3.2 
64
default value of 0% flare efficiency is applied. 
-      If  flaring  temperature  is  between  1,000  and  
1,200°C,   the   default   value   of   90%   flare   
efficiency is applied. 
-      If  flaring  temperature  is  outside  1,000  and  
1,200°C  but  not  below  500°C,  the  default  
value of 50% flare efficiency is applied. 
 
minutes     during     the     hour     h,     but     the     
manufacturer’s      specifications      on      proper      
operation of the flare are not met at any point in 
time during the hour h.  
- 90%, if the temperature in the exhaust gas of the 
flare  (T
flare
)  is  above  500  °C  for  more  than  40  
minutes     during     the     hour     h     and     the     
manufacturer’s      specifications      on      proper      
operation   of   the   flare   are   met   continuously   
during the hour h. “ 
It  is  confirmed  from  the  onsite  interviews  with  the  
operating  team  and  from  document  check  that  the  
enclosed high temperature flare was used during the 
monitoring  period  from  2011-02-26  to  2012-07-31  
more  or  less  as  “emergency  unit”.  This  means  that  
under  normal  conditions,  all  landfill  gas  captured  on  
the Bantargebang Landfill is provided to the project’s 
electricity  generation  facility.  Only  in  a  few  cases  
(e.g. if the total electricity generation facility was not 
operational),  gas  has  been  sent  to  the  enclosed  
high-temperature flare. This events did not occur that 
often,  additionally  they  last  usually  only  for  a  short  
period.   This   can   be   seen   when   comparing   the   
measured  values  of  “Total  amount  of  landfill  gas  
captured”   (=29.708.303   Nm³)   with   the   values   of   
“Amount  of  landfill  gas  combusted   in   flare   unit”   
(=55.035 Nm³). The share of “landfill gas combusted 
in flare unit” represents 0.185 % of the “total amount 
of  landfill  gas  captured”.  As  it  can  be  seen  in  this  
comparison, the amount of LFG flared is very small, 
thus  the  flaring  time  is  very  small  as  well.  So,  it  is  
nearly impossible for Project Participant to apply the 
requirements  as  per  the  tool  because  flaring  events  
with duration of more than 40 minutes are rare. Due 
to   this,   the   Project   Participant   determines   flare   
efficiency  on  minute-by-minute  base,  instead  of  the  
hourly determination in methodology tool. 
Since  the  manufacturer’s  specifications  on  proper  
operation    of    the    flare    is    upon    combustion    
temperature,    and    combustion    temperature    is    
automatically  controlled  by  PLC,  the  requirement  of  
combustion temperature between 1,000 and 1,200°C 
can   be   regarded   as   always   met,   and   the   flare   
efficiency should be just dependend on exhaust gas 

                                 VERIFICATION REPORT: VCS Version 3   
v3.2 
65
temperature: when it is below or equal to 500°C, the 
default   value   of   0%   flare   efficiency   should   be   
applied;  and  when  it  is  above  500  °C,  the  default  
value of 90% flare efficiency should be applied. 
However,   in   PP’s   approach,   the   1000-1200°C   
temperature  check  is  conducted  on  exhaust  gas  
temperature  instead  of  combustion  temperature,  so  
that the flare efficiency in the minute is:   
- 0%  if  the  temperature  in  the  exhaust  gas  of  the  
flare (T
flare
) is below or equal to 500 °C 
- 50%, if the temperature in the exhaust gas of the 
flare (T
flare
) is above 500 °C, but not within 1000-
1200 °C 
- 90%, if the temperature in the exhaust gas of the 
flare (T
flare
) is above 500 °C and it is within 1000-
1200 °C 
This  way,  only  when  exhaust  gas  temperature  is  
1000-1200 °C, flare efficiency is 90%; when it is 500-
1000 °C or 1200 °C above, efficiency is 50%; when it 
is below or equal to 500 °C, efficiency is 0. 
This   is   assessed   as   conservative   and   no-harm,   
because: 
-      exhaust  gas  temperature  is  always  lower  than  
combustion   temperature;   when   exhaust   gas   
temperature   is   above   1000   °C,   combustion   
temperature is also ensured as above 1000 °C; 
-     since  combustion  temperature  is  automatically  
controlled   by   PLC   unit,   the   1000-1200   °C   
combustion  temperature  range  can  be  regarded  
as  always  met.  Also,  flare  PLC/instruments  had  
no malfunctions or errors during working time. 
It  is  worthwhile  to  note  that  as  confirmed  by  the  
manufacturer,  the  flare  is  complying  with  various  
stringent  European  standards  and  additionally  its  
construction resp. its auxiliary equipment guarantees 
minimised emissions. The manufacturer emphasizes 
the typical combustion efficiency of 99.9 % 
/53/
. 
Therefore, the verification team is of the opinion that 

                                 VERIFICATION REPORT: VCS Version 3   
v3.2 
66
the  tool  approach  is  not  feasible  for  this  project’s  
particular situation and the approach followed by the 
Project   Participant   is   practical   and   results   in   
conservative    estimation    of    emission    reduction.    
Therefore, the deviation is accepted. 
 
 
4.2 Accuracy of GHG Emission Reduction or Removal Calculations 
GHG emissions reductions for the project and the baseline scenario were correctly calculated using the 
formulae described in the applied methodology for this project. GLC's Assessment Team has reviewed 
the emission reduction (ER) spreadsheets 
/5/
 and checked all the formulae and found they are correct and 
in line with the monitoring plan of the registered CDM PDD and the applied monitoring methodology. 
The emission reduction due to capturing of methane, its utilisation in onsite gas engines and its 
combustion in an onsite enclosed high temperature flare was estimated by measuring the required 
parameters using appropriate monitoring equipment and using the formulae described in the methodology 
ACM0001 (version 11) and the CDM PDD except the deviation described in the above section. All the 
monitored parameters are described above in section 4.1. All ex-ante parameters which are used in the 
calculation of emission reduction are presented in section 3.1 of the MR transparently. It is confirmed that 
all the ex-ante parameters have been correctly used in the emission reduction calculation.

adopted as 0.8 instead of 1.0 indicated in PDD, which is assessed as reasonable and thus is accepted, 
based on physical inspection of the landfill, which revealed that the project may not satisfy the 
requirement of MCF 1.0. For details please refer to CAR 22.

The  reduction  in  achieved  emission  reduction  is  considered  appropriate  due  to  various  conservative  
approaches  in  the  emission  reduction  calculation,  variation  in  process  parameters  and  uncertainties  
applying models to predict methane generation. However, no justification is required since the achieved 
emission reduction is lower than the estimated value in the CDM PDD. 
 
4.3 Quality of Evidence to Determine GHG Emission Reductions or Removals 
During  the  verification  site  visit,  all  relevant  documents  were  checked  to  assess  the  correctness  and  
quality of data submitted by the project participants, which are used to determine emission reductions. 
Total  amount  of  landfill  gas  captured,  total  amount  of  landfill  gas  fed  to  power  plant,  total  amount  of  
landfill gas fed to flare unit, volumetric fraction of CH
4
 in landfill gas and flare temperature were verified 
with data provided by the project’s data acquisition system. GLC's Assessment Team performed a “data 
authenticity check” in which all available raw data 
/14/
 has been again downloaded from the project’s data 
acquisition  system.  Such  checking  aimed  to  ensure  that  only  authentic/not-modified  monitoring  records  
data were used for the emission reduction calculation (thus ensuring that the measurement records made 
available in the MS-Excel format “raw data” input files and measurement records reported in the monthly 
emission  reduction  spreadsheets  were  not  intentionally  or  unintentionally  edited/modified  during  the  
generation  of  these  files).  The  downloaded  raw  data  in  encrypted  format  
/14/ 
was  handed  over  to  GLC's  
Assessment Team in order to perform the data authenticity check. This check was done in 2 steps. First 
step was to convert the data available in encrypted format 
/14/
 to readable data in MS-Excel format. In a 
second step, the so converted data has been compared against the data presented as “raw data” in the 
ER-spreadsheets 
/5/
. 
As a result of the checks, by comparing files previously generated by the project participants against the 
files generated by the auditors, GLC's Assessment Team was able to confirm that the generated monthly 
data  is  identical  to  the  data  provided  in  the  monthly  emission  reduction  calculation  spreadsheets  
previously  generated  by  the  project  participants  as  part  of  the  monitoring/reporting  process.  While  no  
deviations  or  differences  were  found  when  comparing  the  files,  and  by  assuming  that  the  downloaded  
data  format  is  a  reliable,  un-editable  and  authentic  monitoring  data  (by  taking  for  grant  that  data  earlier  
recorded in the data acquisition unit cannot be edited or modified), the performed data authenticity check 
has   thus   successfully   and   sufficiently   confirmed   that   only   authentic   and   not-modified   monitored   

                                 VERIFICATION REPORT: VCS Version 3   
v3.2 
70
measurement  data  (from  the  project’s  data  acquisition  system)  were  previously  used  by  the  project  
participants for the calculation of emission reductions reported in the Monitoring Report. 
The amount of electricity imported by the Project from the grid and the amount of electricity exported by 
the Project to the grid were verified with the monthly invoices provided by the power grid operator 
/49/
. 
All records needed for monitoring are archived in line with the requirements of the registered monitoring 
plan.  No  significant,  lack  of  evidence  and  missing  data  were  detected  during  onsite  verification.  Hence,  
the verification team confirms that the monitoring system ensures required quality to ensure the quality of 
the  monitored  data.  All  internal  data  are  subjected  to  QA/QC  measures,  which  are  continuously  
developed and improved 
/54/
. 
All  the  meters  (landfillgas  flow  meters,  landfillgas  pressure  meters,  landfillgas  temperature  sensors,  gas  
analyser and electricity meters) were calibrated at appropriate calibration frequency (described in section 
4.1)  to  ensure  the  quality  of  the  data.  In  cases  calibration  was  delayed,  conservative  approaches  have  
been applied. Hence GLC's Assessment Team confirms that the quality of data is reasonably good and 
the emission reductions have been calculated conservatively.  
It was verified through onsite interviews that the plant’s team involved in the monitoring of project activity 
is  well  experienced.  Hence,  the  verification  team  concludes  that  competent  staff  is  employed  by  the  
project proponent to carry out the relevant tasks with sufficient accuracy. Furthermore, it was learnt from 
the  onsite  interviews  with  the  operating  team  that  a  training  was  provided  by  the  manufacturer  of  the  
flaring  station  
/43/
,  this  training  included  the  monitoring  devices  for  LFG  quality,  LFG  quantity,  Flaring  
parameters as well as data acquisition.  
GLC is of the opinion that this method of estimation is accurate and results in conservative estimation of 
emission reduction and is in line with the applicable VCS requirements. 
4.4 Management and Operational System 
GLC's  Assessment  Team  was  able  to  verify  that  authorities  and  responsibilities  for  monitoring  and  
reporting of all data related to the emission reductions were clearly defined for the monitoring period from 
2011-02-26  to  2012-07-31.  Moreover,  all  project  related  equipment  was  confirmed  to  be  operated  by  
qualified  and  trained  staff  
/43/
.  The  frequency  of  monitoring  measurement,  as  well  as  applicable  
calibrations  and  reporting  details  were  conducted  as  outlined  in  the  monitoring  plan  available  in  the  
registered CDM PDD. 
The allocation of the responsibilities is followed as described in the registered VCS PD. Routines for the 
archiving  of  data  are  defined  and  documented.  During  the  site  visit  all  the  required  plant  records  were  
verified and found that the data is consistent with the provided in the VCS-Monitoring Report 
/4/
 and ER 
sheets 
/5/
. 
The monitoring plan described in section 3.3 of the MR is confirmed to be correct. All the parameters of 
the monitoring plan are monitored using appropriate metering system. The parameters related to landfill 
gas  flow,  landfill  gas  methane  content,  flare’s  exhaust  gas  temperature,  electricity  generation  and  
electricity  consumption  are  measured  continuously.  Reporting  and  recording  is  done  on  a  minute-by-
minute  base  (to  the  electronic  data  acquisition  system),  except  for  electricity  generation  and  electricity  
consumption, where it is done on a monthly base. 

                                 VERIFICATION REPORT: VCS Version 3   
v3.2 
71
Available raw data is downloaded daily on site and sent to the Project Participant’s head office, where it is 
stored  and  further  processed.  Data  is  then  available  and  stored  on  site  and  in  the  head  office  as  a  
backup.  It  is  therefore  confirmed  that  the  data  monitoring  and  data  storage  represents  good  monitoring  
practice. 
GLC's Assessment Team has interviewed the plant personnel who are involved in the monitoring of the 
parameters  that  are  used  to  determine  the  emission  reductions  of  the  project  activity.  It  is  confirmed  
based  on  the  interviews  that  the  plant’s  team  is  competent  enough  to  monitor  the  parameters  as  
described in the monitoring plan. 
As  discussed  above,  GLC's  Assessment  Team  concludes  that  management  and  operational  system  of  
the  project  is  implemented  and  operated  well.  Thus  it  ensures  the  quality  of  data  which  is  required  in  
calculating  the  emission  reductions.  Description  of  the  monitoring  plan  including  organisation  structure  
and data management system provided in section 3.3 of the MR is confirmed to be correct. 
 
 
 

                                 VERIFICATION REPORT: VCS Version 3   
v3.2 
72
5          VERIFICATION          CONCLUSION          
Germanischer  Lloyd  Certification  GmbH  (GLC)  has  performed  the  1
st
  verification  of  the  project:  
“Bantargebang  Landfill  Gas  Management  &  Power  Generation”  with  regard  to  the  applicable  relevant  
requirements for VCS project activity. 
The  project  activity  encompasses  the  collection  of  LFG  generated  at  the  Bantargebang  landfill,  its  
destruction  (by  combustion  in  a  high  temperature  enclosed  flare)  and  its  utilization  as  gaseous  fuel  for  
electricity  generation  in  an  electricity  generation  facility.  All  electricity  generated  at  the  electricity  
generation facility is exported through the electricity grid, thus displacing equivalent amount of electricity 
that would otherwise be generated by fossil-fuel sources (power plants) and new additions in the absence 
of  the  project  activity.  For  periods  when  the  electricity  generation  facility  is  not  (fully)  operational  or  for  
periods  when  more  LFG  is  available  than  the  electricity  generation  facility  can  convert  into  power,  one  
enclosed  high  temperature  flare  is  available  for  safe  combustion  of  the  LFG  with  the  goal  of  avoiding  
emissions of methane (CH
4
) into the atmosphere. 
This verification covers the period from 2011-02-26 to 2012-07-31 (including both days). It is noteworthy 
that  due  to  commissioning,  not  all  instruments  and  devices  have  been  in  place  and  fully  operational  on  
the starting date of this monitoring period (2011-02-26). On this date, the electricity generation facility was 
able to export electricity to the grid. This was monitored from the early beginning by the use of electricity 
meters.  The  remaining  instruments  related  to  landfill  gas  flow,  landfill  gas  methane  content  and  flare’s  
exhaust  gas  temperature  have  been  commissioned  in  June  2011.  Thus,  for  the  months  of  February,  
March,  April  and  May  2011,  emission  reductions  from  capture  and  destruction  of  methane  contained  in  
landfill  gas  are  not  claimed.  For  these  months,  only  the  emission  reductions  for  CO
2
-displacement 
(through electricity exported to the grid) are claimed and verified. 
PT  Navigat  Organic  Energy  Indonesia  is  responsible  for  the  collection  of  data  in  accordance  with  the  
validated monitoring plan and the reporting of GHG emissions reductions from the project. 
It is GLC’s responsibility to express an independent verification statement on the reported GHG emission 
reduction from the project. GLC does not express any opinion on the selected baseline scenario or on the 
validated and registered CDM PDD. 
The  scope  of  this  verification  covers  the  determination  of  voluntary  greenhouse  gas  emission  reduction  
generated by the above mentioned project. GLC conducted the verification based on the registered CDM 
PDD 
/15/
,  validation  report  
/6/
,  monitoring  report  
/4/
,  ER  sheets  
/5/
,  the  approved  consolidated  monitoring  
methodology  ACM0001  “Consolidated  baseline  and  monitoring  methodology  for  landfill  gas  project  
activities”  in  its  version  11  and  supporting  documents  made  available  to  the  verifiers  by  the  project  
participants. The verification included: 
i)    Checking  whether  the  design  of  the  project  is  implemented  and  installed  as  planned  and  
described in the registered CDM PDD; 
ii)    Checking  whether  the  provisions  of  the  monitoring  methodology  and  the  monitoring  plan  in  the  
CDM PDD were consistently and appropriately applied; 
iii)   The collection of evidence supporting the reported data; 
iv)   Checking whether the installed monitoring equipment is calibrated appropriately. 

                                 VERIFICATION REPORT: VCS Version 3   
v3.2 
73
As a result of the verification, GLC confirms that 
-      all  operations  of  the  project  are  implemented  and  installed  as  planned  and  described  in  the  
registered CDM PDD, 
-     the  monitoring  system  is  in  place  and  functional  and  is  in  line  with  the  applied  monitoring  
methodology and the monitoring plan, 
-     the  installed  equipment  essential  for  estimating  emission  reductions  works  reliable  and  is  
calibrated appropriately, 
- GHG emission reductions are calculated without significant misstatements in a conservative and 
appropriate manner. 
The verification of reported emission reductions is based on the information made available to GLC and 
the  engagement  conditions  detailed  in  this  report.  Hence,  GLC  cannot  be  held  liable  by  any  party  for  
decisions made or not made based on this report. Also all the documents checked during on-site visit and 
verification  process  will  be  kept  confidential  and  will  not  be  disclosed  without  the  Project  Participant’s  
consent as required by VCSA. 
In GLC’s opinion, the GHG emissions reduction for the “Bantargebang Landfill Gas Management & Power 
Generation”  as  reported  in  the  Monitoring  Report  issued  on  “29  December  2012,  version  3.1”  are  
calculated without material misstatements in a conservative and appropriate manner. The GHG emission 
reductions  were  correctly  calculated  on  the  basis  of  the  approved  consolidated  monitoring  methodology  
ACM0001  “Consolidated  baseline  and  monitoring  methodology  for  landfill  gas  project  activities”  in  its  
version 11 and the monitoring plan contained in the validated CDM PDD for the project. 
Germanischer  Lloyd  Certification  GmbH  herewith  confirms  that  the  project  has  achieved  emission  
reduction during the reporting period from 2011-02-26 to 2012-07-31 (including both days) as follows:

02 November 2012 (1st round): Format of Monitoring Report has been amended in several aspects (fonts, etc.) to comply with the VCS requirement. Including the title page to address the DOE’s concern in this CAR.   
2012-11-14 (1st round): The  revised  VCS  Monitoring  Report  (version  2.0)  has  been  reviewed  by  GLC's  Assessment  Team.  It  can  be  confirmed  that  the  above  mentioned  version  has  been  amended in terms of editorial mistakes and application of the “VCS Monitoring Report Template” in its version 3.1.  In  contrary  to  the  above,  the  revised  VCS  Monitoring  Report  (version  2.0)  shows  a  few  inconsistencies.  The  “Report Version: 1.2” as indicated in the footer from pages 1  to  40  is  not  consistent  to  the  “version  2.0”  as  indicated  in  the  box  of  the  title  page  and  in  the  rest  of  the  document.  Additionally,  the  pagination  of  all  pages  is  not  correct. Finally, the monitoring report title has not been presented in the format as requested by the “VCS Monitoring Report Template” in its version 3.1.  Hence, CAR 1 is still open.

02 November 2012 (1st round): This CAR were issued prior 
to the site visit. During 
validation meeting, we have provided the DOE with full access of technical specifications for our flow metering system (the DeltabarS , Omnigrad TR10, Deltatop, Cerabar M, Energy Manager (RMC621), and Memograph M)  Essentially, the DetltabarS, Omnigrad TR10 and Cerabar M are interconnected by the Deltatop unit, which then send signal to the Energy Manager which calculates the volumetric flow-rate from all input points, and subsequently transmit this signal to the Memograph M for data storing and presentation. This relationship has now been clarified in the VCSMR for the respective parameters.   Please see CAR 19 with regard to how the term “accuracy” are being defined by flow meter manufacturer, and the meaning of term given in the calibration certificates – from the manufacturer perspective.    
2012-11-14 (1st round): Please see GLC’s Assessment to CAR 19! The  presentation  of  the  following  parameters  has  been  reviewed  in  the  revised  VCS  Monitoring  Report  (version  2.0) : 
-
 
LFGtotal,t 
-
 
LFGelectricity,t 
-
 
LFGflare,t 
The  actual  presentation  of  accuracies  cannot  be  deemed  correct  as  this  is  inconsistent  with  Project  Participant’s  answer  (b)  to  CAR  19.  Thus,  the  Maximum  Permissible  Error  has  not  been  applied  in  the  presentation  of  the  above mentioned parameters.  Hence, CAR 6 is still open.

raw data, several issues appear: 
-
 
The time indicated on the calibration protocol does not fit into the presented data and thus cannot be reproduced.

For the time of calibration, data is varying according to calibration procedure. It is not stated how this has been taken into account while calculating the emission reductions. 
 
field title) should be interpreted as the “report time” rather than the “calibration time” 
The precise time of the calibration would be those recorded / indicated by the Memograph. All spreadsheet now indicates the period of which the gas sensors were undergoing calibration (“in-calibration”).  (b)
 
The period of which the gas analyzers are being calibrated is now clearly indicated in the spreadsheet. During this period, no emission reduction from methane abatement is claimed (MDproject = 0)   
and time, the exact time of calibration can be reproduced by Project Participant’s data logging system. The gas analyzer has a 2-position-key switch. Position 1 is in
dicated as “Measuring”, 
while position 2 shows “Calibrate”. The position of the key is registered as digital value in the data log. Position 1 gi
ves the signal “o.k.”, 
position 2 gives “Cal”. By using this information, calibration periods can be identified. As raw data coming from the data logging system is not editable (and must be converted into a readable spreadsheet by using a special software), the information of calibration events can be traced. 
(b)
 
This approach of Project Participant has been assessed by GLC's Assessment Team. As the real value of methane (CH4) for the calibration-period is not registered, Project Participant prefers not to claim any emission reduction. This is conservative. The above described way to distinguish times with and without calibration has been formalized by Project Participant and whenever the status “calibration” is registered, the value for MDproject,p is indicated as zero, so no emission reduction is claimed. 
 Hence, CAR 16 is closed.

CAR 19 (2012-10-19) Some    of    the    presented    calibration    protocols  of  the  instruments  used  for  monitoring   purposes   are   showing   a   higher   deviation   than   the   maximum   permissible      error      set      by      the      manufacturer.
